Eggeling
  1. Now, on the third, or the sixth, or the twelfth day 1, having combined (the two performances of) the Pravargya and Upasads 2, he ‘sets out 3’ the Pravargya, for set out (removed), as it were, is this head (from the trunk). Having gathered together all around it 4 (the MahƒÅvƒ´ra pot), they

meet together upon the Vedi in the ≈öƒÅlƒÅ, (entering) by the front door.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. The ƒÄgnƒ´dhra then brings three bundles of faggots to the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya, and kindling one of them, he offers (thereon) whilst holding it 5 on a level with (the Sacrificer’s) mouth. When the sacrifice had its head cut off its heat went out of it, and entered these worlds: it is with that heat he thus supplies and completes it.

(‡§ò‡•ç‡§®·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â) ‡§â‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§ò‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§∏‡•å·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç[[!!]] ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§Ø‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Å‡§ö‡§æ ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§â‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§ò‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§∏‡•å·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§Ø‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§õ‡•Å‡§ö‡§æ 6 ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. And as to why (it is held) on a level with the mouth,–well, what is level with the mouth is, as it were, above; and above, as it were, is yonder (heavenly) world: thus he thereby supplies and completes it (the Pravargya) with that heat which had entered yonder world.

‡•¶‡•™

Eggeling
  1. [He offers, with VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 18,] ‘What heavenly fire of thine there is, O Gharma,’–just the fire which is heavenly;–‘what is in the GƒÅyatrƒ´ and in the HavirdhƒÅna,’–

just that which is in the GƒÅyatrƒ´ (metre) and HavirdhƒÅna (shed);–‘may that (fire) of thine increase and become firm: to that (fire) of thine, hail!’ in this there is nothing hidden, so to speak.

Eggeling
  1. Then, having kindled the second (bundle), he offers (thereon) whilst holding it navel-high; for in the middle, as it were, is what is navel-high, and in the middle, as it were, is the air-world: thus he thereby supplies and completes it with that heat which had entered the air-world.

Eggeling
  1. ‘What fire of thine is in the air,’–just the fire which is in the air;–‘what is in the Trish·π≠ubh and in the ƒÄgnƒ´dhra,’ just that which is in the Trish·π≠ubh (metre) and ƒÄgnƒ´dhra (fire-shed);–‘may that (fire) of thine increase and become firm: to that (fire) of thine, hail!’ in this there is nothing hidden, so to speak.

Eggeling
  1. Then, having put the third (bundle) on the fire, he offers on it whilst sitting; for below, as it were, is he who is sitting; and below, as it were, is this (terrestrial) world: thus the thereby supplies and completes it with that heat which had entered this (terrestrial) world.

‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú·≥ò‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø[[!!]] ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§ú·≥ò‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏‡§¶·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò ‡§§·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§Ü·≥ò‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú·≥ò‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡•ó ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§ú·≥ò‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¶‡•ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò ‡§§·≥ò‡§Ü·≥ò‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. ‘What fire of thine is in the earth,’–just that fire which is in the earth;–‘what is in the Jagatƒ´ and in the Sadas,’ just that which is in the Jagatƒ´ (metre) and the Sadas (shed);–‘may that (fire) of thine increase and become firm: to that (fire) of thine, hail!’ in this there is nothing hidden, so to speak.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He (the Adhvaryu) then steps out 7, with

(VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 19), ‘Thee (we will follow) for the protection of the Kshatra,’–for he who shines yonder 8 is indeed the divine ruler: ‘for the protection of this human ruler,’ he thereby means to say;–‘guard thou the Brahman’s body!’–that is to say, ‘preserve thou the Brahman’s person (ƒÅtman);’–‘Thee (we will follow) as a stay for the Vi≈õ,’–the Vi≈õ (people, clan) doubtless is the sacrifice: ‘for the safety of the sacrifice,’ he thus means to say;–‘we will follow to new prosperity,’–it is for the safety and the stability of the sacrifice that the says this.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then says (to the PrastotrÃ•), ‘Sing the SƒÅman!’ or ‘Recite the SƒÅman!’ but let him rather say, ‘Sing the SƒÅman!’ for they indeed sing the SƒÅman. When he sings the SƒÅman it is in order that the fiends, the Rakshas, should not injure these

outside the sacrifice, the body; for the SƒÅman is a repeller of the fiends, the Rakshas.

Eggeling
  1. He sings it on a (verse) relating to Agni, for Agni is the repeller of the Rakshas. On an Aticchandas (verse) he sings it, for that–to wit, the Aticchandas (redundant metre) is all metres, therefore he sings it on an Aticchandas (verse).

  1. He sings 10, ‘Agni burneth, encountereth with flames, AhƒÅvo! AhƒÅvo 10!’–it is thus he repels the fiends, the Rakshas, from here.

Eggeling

(‡§§‡•ç‡§§) ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑·≥ò ‡§∂‡•Å‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ã·≥ò ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•Å·≥ò‡§ó‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶·≥ò‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§™‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•Å·≥ò‡§ó‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§• ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶·≥ò‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§•‡•ã ‡§π·≥ò ‡§®‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ã·≥ò ‡§π‡§ø‡§®·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø·≥ò ‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶·≥ò‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ã ‡§®·≥ò ‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§• ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ü·≥ò‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®·≥ò ‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§Ω‡§â·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Let him ‘set out’ that (Pravargya) on an island; for, when heated, it becomes burning-hot 12; and were he to set it out on this (earth), its heat would enter this (earth); and were he to set it out on water, its heat would enter the water; but when he sets it out on an island–thus, indeed, it does not injure either the water or this (earth), for inasmuch as he does not throw it into the water, it does not injure the water; and inasmuch as the water flows all round it–water being a means

of soothing–it does not injure this (earth): let him therefore set it out on an island.

‡•ß‡•´

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§ø·≥ò‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. But let him rather set it out on the Uttaravedi 13; for the Uttara-vedi is the sacrifice, and the Pravargya is its head: he thus restores to the sacrifice its head.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. The first Pravargya (pot) he sets out so as to be close to (the front side of) the navel (of the Uttara-vedi), for the northern (upper) navel is the voice, and the Pravargya is the head: he thus places the voice in the head.

Eggeling
  1. [He does so, with VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 20,] ‘The four-cornered,’–four-cornered, indeed, is he who shines yonder, for the quarters are his corners: therefore he says, ‘Four-cornered’;–

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. –‘Mighty navel of the divine order,’–the divine order being the truth, he thereby means to say, ‘The mighty navel of the truth;’–’that mighty one (be) unto us of all life;’–’that mighty one (be) unto us (a bestower) of the complete (term of) life,’ he thereby means to say 14;

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. –‘from the hatred, from the guile,’–in this there is nothing hidden, so to speak;–‘of him of another law, let us free ourselves!’–another law, indeed, is his (Pravargya’s and the Sun’s), and another that of men 15: therefore he says, ‘Of him of another law, let us free ourselves.’ In this way the other two (pots are placed) east of it: this is threefold, for the head is threefold 16.

‡•®‡•¶

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

‡§™‡•Å‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É·≥ò‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡••
(‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠) ‡§Æ‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•å·≥ò ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è·≥ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§É ‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•á ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§π·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§ö‡•å ‡§π·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§™‡•Å‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Æ‡•É·≥ò‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡••
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•å·≥ò ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç·≥ò ‡§è‡•ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§É ‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•á ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§π·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§ö‡•å ‡§π·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. In front thereof (he places) the reserve (lump of) clay, whereby he puts flesh upon it (Pravargya); on the two sides thereof the two lifting-sticks, whereby he gives two arms to it; and on the two sides yet further away the two Rauhi·πáa offering-ladles, whereby he gives two hands to it.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. On the left (north) side (he places) the spade, for there is its place of rest; on the right (right) side the imperial throne, for there is its place of rest; on the left side the black antelope-skin, for there is its place of rest; on all sides (save the front side) the fans, for, the fans being the vital airs, he thereby bestows vital airs on it; there are three of them, for there are three vital airs, the out- (and in-) breathing, the up-breathing, and the through-breathing: it is these he thus bestows on him.

Eggeling
  1. He then puts the cords and halter on the supporting-tray, and places (the latter) behind (the

navel) with its point towards the east: a belly he thus gives to it. On the two sides thereof the two milking-bowls (pinvana): two testicles he thereby gives to it, for by means of his testicles the male overflows (pinv). Behind (them he places) the post and peg: whereby he gives two thighs to it; behind (them) the two Rauhi·πáa-plates, whereby he gives two knees to it; and as to their being single plates, it is because these knees consist, as it were, of single plates (bones). Behind (them) the two poking-sticks (dhrÃ•sh·π≠i), whereby he gives two feet to it, for with the feet one strikes out boldly (dhrÃ•sh·π≠am). On the left side the two mounds 18 used in the performance,. for there is their place of rest; on the right side the MƒÅrjƒÅlƒ´ya 19, for there is its place of rest.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then pours milk into that (chief pot), with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 21), ‘This, O Gharma, is the contents of thy bowels,’–the contents of the bowels being food, it is food he thus puts into it;–‘Grow thou, and fill out thereby!’–in this there is nothing hidden, so to speak;–‘and may we ourselves grow, and fill out!’–it is a blessing he thereby invokes.

Eggeling
  1. Let him not pour in all (the milk), lest the food should turn away from the Sacrificer.–He leaves over half of it or more; and on that same afternoon he pours it to the fast-milk, and hands it to the Sacrificer: thereby he bestows food upon

the Sacrificer, and thus, indeed, food does not turn away from the Sacrificer,

Eggeling
  1. He then sprinkles it (the Pravargya apparatus) with water: water being a means of appeasement, he thus appeases it; he sprinkles it all over: all over he thus appeases it; three times he sprinkles, for threefold is the sacrifice.

Eggeling
  1. He (the Sacrificer) then steps out towards the north-east, with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 24), ‘From out of the gloom have we risen,’–gloom is

evil: it is gloom, evil, he thus drives away;–‘beholding the higher light,’–this (terrestrial) world is higher than the water: it is on this world he thus establishes himself;–‘God S≈´rya, with the gods, the highest light,’–S≈´rya, the highest light, is the heavenly world: it is in the heavenly world he thus finally establishes himself. He walks along without looking back, and puts a log of wood on the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya 24, with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 25), ‘A kindler thou art, fire thou art: lay thou fire into me!’ it is a blessing he thereby invokes.

Eggeling
  1. And at a continued pressing of Soma they also perform the Gharma of curds and whey (Dadhi-gharma),–for Soma is the sacrifice, and the Pravargya is its head: he thus restores to the sacrifice its head,–at the midday-pressing, for that–to wit, the midday-pressing–is Indra’s special pressing: he thus pleases him in his own share;–when the MƒÅdhyandina-pavamƒÅna has been chanted, for the MƒÅdhyandina-pavamƒÅna is the breath: it is breath he thereby lays into him;–with the Agnihotra-ladle, for the Agnihotra is the mouth of sacrifices: he thus puts a mouth in the head.

Eggeling
  1. On its being brought, he says, ‘HotƒÅr, speak what thou hast to speak!’ for the HotrÃ• speaks on this occasion. Then, stepping up, he says, ‘Cooked is the offering-food;’ for cooked, indeed, it is. Having stepped across (behind the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya), and called for the ≈örausha·π≠, he says, ‘Pronounce the offering-formula!’ and offers on the Vasha·π≠ being uttered. When the Vasha·π≠ is

repeated, he brings the draught, and hands it to the Sacrificer.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Having solicited an invitation 27 (and received an answer from the priests), he drinks of it, with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 27), ‘May there be in me that great energy,’–a great energy, indeed, is he who shines yonder;–‘in me the fitness, in me the intelligence,’–fitness and intelligence he thus secures to himself;–’the Gharma of triple fires shineth,’–for this Gharma of triple fires indeed shines;–’together with the shining light,’–for together with the shining light (the sun) it indeed is;–’together with the fire, the Brahman,’–for together with the fire, the Brahman, it indeed is,–(VƒÅj. S. XXXVIII, 28), ‘The seed of the milk hath been brought,’–for this is indeed the seed of the milk that has been brought;–‘may we obtain the milking thereof year after year!’–it is a blessing he thereby invokes. They then cleanse themselves at the pit the significance of this is the same as before.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Now, then, as to the sacrificial gifts. The gold plate he gives to the Brahman; for the Brahman is seated, and gold is settled 28 glory: therefore he gives the gold plate to the Brahman.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. And that cow which yielded the Gharma-milk he gives to the Adhvaryu; for scorched, as it were, is the Gharma, and the Adhvaryu comes forth (from the sacrificial ground) like something scorched 30: therefore he gives it to the Adhvaryu.

Eggeling
  1. And that cow which yielded the Sacrificer’s

fast-milk he gives to the HotrÃ•; for the HotrÃ• is the sacrifice, and the Sacrificer also is the sacrifice: therefore he gives it to the HotrÃ•.

Eggeling
  1. And that cow which yielded the fast-milk for the (Sacrificer’s) wife he gives to the chanters, for it is they, the UdgƒÅtrÃ•s, that do, as it were, the wife’s work on this occasion: therefore he gives it to the chanters.

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡•• (‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ü·≥ò) ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø[[!!]] ‡§Ø·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§§‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•Å ‡§µ‡§æ[[!!]] ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑·≥ò‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ[[!!]] ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•É·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•å‡••

Eggeling
  1. And, verily, whosoever either teaches, or partakes of, this (Pravargya) enters that life, and that light: the observance thereof is the same as at the creation 31.

  1. 493:2 That is, according to whether there are three, six, or twelve Upasad days to the particular form of Soma-sacrifice about to be performed. On each of these days there would be two performances of the Upasads,–and in case the Pravargya is to be performed–as many performances of that sacrifice. ↩︎

  2. 493:3 On the day before the Soma-sacrifice, the two performances of the Pravargya and the Upasads are combined and gone through in the forenoon, instead of the forenoon and afternoon as is otherwise the case. KƒÅty. XXVI, 7, 1 does not refer to the performance of the Pravargya on this day, but merely remarks that ‘at the end of the Upasads (i.e. of the combination of the Upasads, comm.) the removal of the Pravargya’ takes place. ƒÄpast. XV, 12, 4-6, on the other hand, states distinctly that the total number of performances of the Pravargya is to be double that of the Upasad days. ↩︎

  3. 493:4 The ‘setting out’ (utsƒÅdana) of the Pravargya is the technical phrase for the removal and orderly laying out (in the form of a man) of the apparatus used for the Pravargya ceremony. ↩︎

  4. 493:5 After collecting the implements they take them out of the ≈õƒÅlƒÅ and lay them down near the Anta·∏•pƒÅtya peg, at a few steps from the front door (whilst ƒÄpast. makes them to be put on the throne-seat placed north of the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya). ↩︎

  5. 494:1 According to the comm. on KƒÅty. XXVI, 7, 4, it is the Adhvaryu who–after ladling four times into the offering-spoon–distributes this ghee successively over the three bundles of sticks,–viz. pouring some upon the first two whilst they are held, at the specified height over the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya fire, by the Agnƒ´dh (who immediately after the offering throws them into the fire), and upon the third after it has been held knee-high by the Agnƒ´dh, and then thrown into the fire by the Adhvaryu. According to ƒÄpastamba, who makes the PratiprasthƒÅtrÃ• and Adhvaryu the two performers, the third portion of the ghee is offered on the bundle of sticks whilst it is still held knee-high over the fire. As noted by KƒÅtyƒÅyana, the ceremony is analogous (though reversed as regards the order of height) to the offering on the three enclosing-stones at the ≈öatarudriya ceremony, IX, 1, 1, 5 seqq. ↩︎

  6. ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï·≥´ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò A. ↩︎

  7. 495:1 Viz. out of the ≈õƒÅlƒÅ, with the Sacrificer’s wife in front of him, and followed by the others. According to ƒÄpast. XV, 13, 4, the PratiprasthƒÅtrÃ• now leads the Sacrificer’s wife within the enclosure; and whilst attendants carry away the objects not immediately connected with the Pravargya ceremony (post, peg, strings, sand, &c.), the Adhvaryu places the throne-seat (with the chief vessels) so as to stand with two feet on the Vedi, and with the other two outside it, and calls on the PrastotrÃ• to sing the SƒÅman. This (as is usual in chanting) is done three times–the Adhvaryu, however, repeating his summons each time–and each time all of them (including the Patnƒ´) sing or utter a special finale,–the first time in the ≈õƒÅlƒÅ, the second time midway between the ≈õƒÅlƒÅ and the Uttaravedi, and the third time when they have arrived behind the Uttaravedi; the finales corresponding to the formulas of this paragraph, viz.–‘For the protection (or protector) of heaven (we follow) thee!’–‘For the protection of the Brahman–thee!’–‘For the protection of the self–thee!’ ↩︎

  8. 496:1 It should be borne in mind that the MahƒÅvƒ´ra by which they are supposing themselves to be led now, is looked upon as a symbol of the sun. ↩︎

  9. ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä A. ↩︎

  10. 497:1 The same SƒÅman is sung when they betake themselves to the expiatory bath at the end of the Soma-sacrifice, cf. IV, 4, 5, 8 where the stobha had better be altered to ‘ahƒÅvo’ (though the Sandhi in the text is the same as of ‘ahƒÅvas’). As on that former occasion, all the priests, as well as the Sacrificer, join in the finale. ↩︎ ↩︎

  11. 497:2 In doing so, they take the Pravargya-vessels and implements along with them. ↩︎

  12. 497:3 Hardly ‘is suffering pain,’ as it was taken at IX, 2, 1, 29; though ‘≈õu≈õucƒÅna’ and ‘≈õuc’ evidently refer to internal heat, or passion, cf. p. 464, note 4 , p. 468, note 1. ↩︎

  13. 498:1 KƒÅtyƒÅyana only lays down the rule that, in the case of the sacrifice not being accompanied with the building of a fire-altar, the Pravargya apparatus should be removed to the Uttara-vedi; whilst, in the case of one who likewise performs the Agnicayana, he would doubtless follow the indication already laid down in the BrƒÅhma·πáa, IX, 2, 1, 19; viz. that the pot may be removed to an island, but should rather be deposited on the fire-altar (in which case, however, the ‘setting out’ of the apparatus would apparently have to be deferred till after the performance of the Soma-sacrifice). ƒÄpastamba treats of the Uttara-vedi as the place where the implements are to be deposited, but finally he allows an option of other places, including an island, but not the fire-altar. ↩︎

  14. 498:2 The words ‘sa na·∏• sarvƒÅyu·∏• saprathƒÅ·∏•,’ being here used as explanatory of ‘sa no vi≈õvƒÅyu·∏• saprathƒÅ·∏•,’ have probably got by mistake into the Sa·πÅhitƒÅ. ↩︎

  15. 499:1 The author evidently understands the text more in accordance with Mahƒ´dhara’s interpretation which makes ‘anyavratasya’ to refer to the Supreme Spirit (paramƒÅtmƒÅ) whose law, or ways, are different front men’s, and construes it with ‘sa≈õcima’ (we serve, are devoted, to that righteous one). The preceding part of the half-verse he would thus take independently of this:–‘Away hatred! away guile!’ ↩︎

  16. 499:2 Viz. consisting of bone, skin, and hair. ↩︎

  17. ‡§µ‡•É·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á A. - ibid. ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•É·≥ò‡§∑‡•Ä A. E. - ibid. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡•å A. ↩︎

  18. 500:1 That is, the sand used for them, and brought thither in vessels. ↩︎

  19. 500:2 That is, the sand of the ‘mound of remains’ (ucchish·π≠akhara), see p. 489, note 3. ↩︎

  20. ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§π‡§∞·≥´ A. ↩︎

  21. 501:1 Or, bull.–The VƒÅj. S. (XXXVIII, 22) here inserts the verse Rig-v.   22. 501:2 KƒÅty. XXVI, 7, 36 (doubtless in accordance with another ≈õƒÅkhƒÅ) also prescribes here the Ish·π≠ƒÅhotrƒ´ya SƒÅman. ↩︎
